      1 # CLAUDE.md
      2 
      3 This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when 
        working with code in this repository.
      4 
      5 ## What This Is
      6 
      7 Patrona is a **UI prototype** for a geriatric care management (GC
        M) platform. It's a single-page React app that runs entirely in t
        he browser with no build step — React 18, ReactDOM, and Babel Sta
        ndalone are loaded from CDNs, and JSX files are transpiled client
        -side via `<script type="text/babel">`.
      8

⏺ User approved Claude's plan
  ⎿  Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/structured-munching-whale.md · /plan to edit
     Plan: AI-Powered Care Note Synthesis

     Context

     Patrona currently mocks all AI generation — post-visit notes, call capture
     summaries, and intake synthesis all use hardcoded data with fake delays.
     The goal is to wire up real LLM-powered summarization so the text input
     actually drives the output.

     Architecture

     API Proxy (required)

     Can't call Claude API directly from the browser (CORS blocks it, and API
     keys would be exposed in source). Need a thin proxy:

     - Recommended: Cloudflare Worker — zero infra, free tier (100k req/day),
     ~40 lines of code, npx wrangler deploy
     - Alternative: local Node script — for pure-local dev, avoids any
     deployment
     - Single endpoint: POST /api/generate — receives request from browser,
     attaches API key from secret, forwards to Anthropic, returns response

     Structured Output via Tool Use

     Use Claude's tool_use (function calling) to guarantee structured JSON
     output matching existing schemas. Define one tool per flow with
     tool_choice: { type: "tool", name: "..." } to force it. No need to parse
     free text.

     No Streaming for Phase 1

     Existing progress animations cover the 2-4 second wait naturally. Streaming
      tool_use adds parsing complexity that isn't worth it for a prototype.

     New File: ai.jsx

     Create /Users/fling/Documents/GCM/ai.jsx, loaded between data.jsx and
     shell.jsx in index.html. Contains:
     - window.patronaGenerate(flow, payload) — main function
     - System prompts for each flow
     - Tool schema definitions
     - buildUserMessage(flow, payload) — assembles client context
     - Config: window.PATRONA_CONFIG = { apiUrl: '', useMockData: true } — falls
      back to mock data when no API configured

     Three Flows to Wire Up

     Flow 1: ClientNotesView (simplest — start here)

     Files: views.jsx (generate function ~line 620)
     Input: postVisitNotes text + client profile (diagnoses, meds, care plan,
     previous visit notes)
     Output schema: { caseNote: string, todos: [{ text, priority }] } — matches
     existing VISIT_GENERATED
     Change: Replace setTimeout mock with patronaGenerate('visit-note', { notes,
      client, previousNotes })
     Rendering: No changes needed — already renders from { caseNote, todos }
     shape

     Flow 2: CallCapture (medium — needs refactor)

     Files: capture.jsx (end function ~line 46, GeneratedNotes ~line 237)
     Input: Transcript array serialized to text + client profile + caller
     identity
     Output schema: { summary: string, keyFacts: [{ label, value, change?, 
     trend? }], tasks: [{ title, due, priority }] }
     Change: Replace hardcoded setExtractedTasks + refactor GeneratedNotes to
     render summary/keyFacts from data instead of hardcoded JSX (lines 263-275
     are hardcoded today)

     Flow 3: IntakeView (most complex output)

     Files: intake.jsx (generate ~line 13, IntakeSummary/IntakePlan ~lines
     155-205)
     Input: Intake notes text + client demographics
     Output schema: { summary: { livingSituation, functionalLimits, 
     familyDynamics, immediateRisks[], openQuestions[] }, carePlan: [{ goal, 
     interventions[], timeframe, source }], tasks: [{ text, owner, due, 
     priority, source }] } — matches INTAKE_GENERATED
     Change: Replace staged progress mock with real API call (keep animation as
     cosmetic). Pass response to child components as props instead of reading
     window.INTAKE_GENERATED
     Note: Source citations require prompt to include verbatim quotes from input
      notes

     Prompt Strategy

     Each flow's system prompt:
     - Role: "You are Patrona, an AI assistant for geriatric care managers"
     - Task: specific to flow (draft case note, summarize call, synthesize
     intake)
     - Guard: "Do not provide medical advice. Flag anything requiring physician
     review."
     - Output: "Call the provided tool with your response"

     User message: concatenate client context fields + the actual input text

     Implementation Order

     1. Proxy setup (30 min) — Cloudflare Worker or local Node proxy
     2. ai.jsx helper (1 hr) — shared generation function, prompts, tool schemas
     3. ClientNotesView (1 hr) — simplest flow, proves the pipeline works
     4. CallCapture (2-3 hr) — requires GeneratedNotes refactor from hardcoded
     to data-driven
     5. IntakeView (2-3 hr) — most complex output schema, source citations need
     care
     6. Polish (1 hr) — error handling, mock/live toggle in tweaks panel

     Verification

     - Set PATRONA_CONFIG.useMockData = true → existing mock behavior works
     unchanged
     - Set PATRONA_CONFIG.useMockData = false + valid apiUrl → real API calls
     - Type post-visit notes for Arthur → generate → case note references actual
      typed content
     - Run call capture → end → summary reflects transcript content
     - Paste intake notes → generate → care plan cites actual quotes from notes

⏺ Background command "Start Node server" completed (exit code 0)

⏺ Server is running. Refresh http://localhost:8080 to test. Here's a summary of
  everything that was built:

  What's done:

  1. server.js — Local Node dev server that serves static files and proxies
  /api/generate to the Anthropic API. Run with ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-... node 
  server.js to enable real AI, or just node server.js for mock mode.
  2. ai.jsx — AI generation layer with:
    - window.patronaGenerate(flow, payload) — async function that calls the API
  or returns null for mock mode
    - System prompts for all 3 flows (visit-note, call-capture, intake)
    - Tool schemas matching existing output structures exactly
    - buildUserMessage() that assembles client context + input text
    - window.PATRONA_CONFIG — flip useMockData: false to enable real API calls
  3. ClientNotesView (views.jsx) — generate() now calls
  patronaGenerate('visit-note', ...), falls back to mock data, shows error with
  retry button on failure
  4. CallCapture (capture.jsx) — end() calls patronaGenerate('call-capture', 
  ...), GeneratedNotes now renders summary and keyFacts from data props instead
  of hardcoded JSX
  5. IntakeView (intake.jsx) — generate() calls patronaGenerate('intake', ...),
  progress animation runs cosmetically in parallel, IntakeSummary and IntakePlan
   accept data props with fallback to window.INTAKE_GENERATED

  To activate real AI: Set useMockData: false in ai.jsx and start the server
  with your API key:
  ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-... node server.js

      43 +## AI Generation                                               
      44 +                                                               
      45 +Three flows use `window.patronaGenerate(flow, payload)` from `a
         +i.jsx`:                                                        
      46 +                                                               
      47 +- **`visit-note`** — ClientNotesView post-visit notes → `{ case
         +Note, todos[] }`. Used in `views.jsx`.                         
      48 +- **`call-capture`** — Call transcript → `{ summary, keyFacts[]
         +, tasks[] }`. Used in `capture.jsx`. `GeneratedNotes` component
         + renders summary/keyFacts from a data prop (not hardcoded).    
      49 +- **`intake`** — Intake notes → `{ summary, carePlan[], tasks[]
         + }`. Used in `intake.jsx`. `IntakeSummary` and `IntakePlan` acc
         +ept data props with fallback to `window.INTAKE_GENERATED`.     
      50 +                                                               
      51 +All flows use Claude's `tool_use` for structured JSON output. W
         +hen `PATRONA_CONFIG.useMockData` is `true` (default), `patronaG
         +enerate` returns `null` and callers use hardcoded mock data fro
         +m `data.jsx`. When `false`, it POSTs to `/api/generate` which `
         +server.js` proxies to the Anthropic API.

❯ /usage

❯ i want to try it with the ai model where do i get the key?                    

⏺ You'll need an Anthropic API key. Here's how to get one:

  1. Go to console.anthropic.com
  2. Sign up or log in
  3. Go to Settings → API Keys
  4. Click Create Key and copy it

  Then run:
  ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=sk-ant-... node server.js

  And flip the flag in ai.jsx line 4 from useMockData: true to useMockData: 
  false.

  Note: There's a small cost per generation (~$0.01–0.03 per call using Claude
  Sonnet). You'll need to add billing/credits to your Anthropic account.

     Plan: Rethink Workspace Section + Client Page Tabs

     Context

     The sidebar Workspace section currently mixes care manager-level tools
     (tasks, time & billing) with per-client views (notes, call capture,
     timeline, care plan). The user wants to separate these: Workspace stays for
      CM-only aggregate tools, and per-client views move into a tabbed client
     page.

     Changes

     1. Sidebar Workspace — CM-only tools

     File: shell.jsx (lines 9-16)

     Replace the current workspace array with:
     { id: 'tasks', label: 'Tasks', icon: 'check' }
     { id: 'time', label: 'Time & billing', icon: 'receipt' }
     { id: 'calendar', label: 'Calendar', icon: 'calendar' }
     { id: 'inbox', label: 'Inbox', icon: 'inbox' }

     Remove from workspace: notes, capture, timeline, careplan — these become
     tabs within the client page.

     2. Client page with tabs

     File: views.jsx — modify ClientNotesView

     When a client is selected and view is 'notes', show a tabbed client page.
     The tabs:
     - Notes (default) — current post-visit notes + generate flow + summary +
     tasks (what ClientNotesView does now)
     - Call capture — embed the existing CallCapture component
     - Timeline — embed the existing TimelineView component
     - Care plan — embed the existing CarePlanView component

     Implementation: Add a clientTab state inside ClientNotesView (or rename to
     ClientPage). Render a tab bar at the top, and switch between the existing
     components based on selected tab. The components already exist and accept
     client as a prop.

     3. New placeholder views for Calendar and Inbox

     File: views.jsx

     Add simple placeholder components:
     - CalendarView — card with placeholder text "Calendar view coming soon" +
     mock upcoming events list
     - InboxView — card with placeholder text "Inbox coming soon" + a few mock
     message rows

     4. Wire up new views in app.jsx

     File: app.jsx (lines 82-90)

     Add routing for calendar and inbox views. Remove routing for capture,
     timeline, careplan as standalone views (they now live inside the client
     page).

     Update viewLabel map to include calendar: 'Calendar' and inbox: 'Inbox',
     remove capture, timeline, careplan.

     5. Update sidebar client click behavior

     Currently clicking a client in the sidebar does setView('notes'). This
     still works — it navigates to the client page which defaults to the Notes
     tab.

     Files to modify

     - shell.jsx — workspace nav items
     - views.jsx — wrap client views in tabbed ClientPage, add CalendarView and
     InboxView placeholders
     - app.jsx — view routing and viewLabel map

     Verification

     - Click "Today" → dashboard loads
     - Click a client in sidebar → tabbed client page with Notes tab active
     - Switch between Notes / Call capture / Timeline / Care plan tabs within
     client page
     - Click Tasks, Time & billing, Calendar, Inbox in workspace → each loads
     correctly
     - Calendar and Inbox show placeholder content
  ⎿  Allowed by PermissionRequest hook

⏺ Here's a summary you can share:

  ---
  Patrona Prototype Updates — April 21

  New: Client Page with Tabs
  When you click into any client, you now get a tabbed page with four views:
  Notes, Call capture, Timeline, and Care plan — all in one place instead of
  scattered across the sidebar.

  New: Post-Visit Notes with AI Generation
  Each client's Notes tab has a post-visit notes section where you can type or
  dictate observations. Hit "Generate case note & to-dos" and it drafts a
  professional case note and extracts actionable tasks. Currently using mock
  data, but wired up to use Claude's API — just needs an API key to go live.

  New: Dashboard (Today View)
  The Today screen is now a proper care manager dashboard: flags needing
  attention, upcoming calls, a full client roster table (click any row to jump
  into that client), draft messages, and a summary of what Patrona automated
  that morning.

  New: Workspace Section
  The sidebar now separates care manager tools (Tasks, Time & billing, Calendar,
   Inbox) from per-client views. Calendar and Inbox are stubbed out with
  realistic mock data.

  New: AI Integration Layer
  Built ai.jsx (shared generation logic with prompts and structured output
  schemas) and server.js (local dev server + Claude API proxy). Three flows are
  wired up: post-visit notes, call capture summaries, and intake synthesis.
  Toggle useMockData to switch between mock and live AI.

  Data & Client Updates
  - Renamed Margaret Holloway → Edith Holloway (to avoid confusion with Margaret
   Okafor)
  - Fleshed out mock data for all 5 clients: medications, care plans, tasks,
  time entries, post-visit notes
  - Added "+" button placeholder explaining client onboarding is in progress

  Running It
  node server.js
  # open http://localhost:8080

❯ make sure when one thing is clicked on the sidebar it removes the highlight   
  for the previous things clicked                                               

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ The issue is that activeView and activeClient are independent — clicking a
  client highlights it but doesn't unhighlight the workspace/overview nav items
  (since activeView might still be 'tasks' etc.), and vice versa. The view is
  'notes' when a client is selected, but workspace items check activeView === 
  n.id.

  The fix: when a workspace/overview item is clicked, the client highlight
  should clear. When a client is clicked, the workspace highlight should clear.
  Since activeView is 'notes' when viewing a client, I just need the nav items
  to also check that the view isn't 'notes', and client rows to check the view
  is 'notes'.

  ⎿  Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/structured-munching-whale.md · /plan to edit
     Plan: Rework Client Page Layout

     Context

     Currently the client page is a flat tab bar (Notes, Call capture, Timeline,
      Care plan) that replaces the top bar. The user wants a proper client
     dashboard as the landing page with the client name prominently at the top,
     a summary of the most relevant info, and a secondary sidebar nav to access
     the other sections.

     Layout

     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
     │  Client Header (name, age, status, avatar)      │
     ├────────┬────────────────────────────────────────┤
     │ Sub-   │                                        │
     │ nav    │  Content area                          │
     │        │                                        │
     │ Dash   │  (Dashboard / Notes / Call capture /   │
     │ Notes  │   Timeline / Care plan)                │
     │ Calls  │                                        │
     │ Time   │                                        │
     │ Care   │                                        │
     │        │                                        │
     └────────┴────────────────────────────────────────┘

     Client Header (persistent across all sub-pages)

     - Avatar, client name (large), age, city, relation
     - Status tag (e.g. "Stable", "Needs attention")
     - Sits at top of the content area, always visible

     Secondary Sidebar Nav

     - Vertical nav inside the content area (left side, narrow ~160px)
     - Items: Dashboard (default), Notes, Call capture, Timeline, Care plan
     - Styled like the main sidebar nav items but smaller/lighter

     Dashboard Tab (new, default landing)

     Pull the most useful info from ClientNotesView's current summary section:
     - Flagged care plan goals (urgent items)
     - Medication alerts (refill-soon, monitor)
     - Recent activity (last 3 items from POST_VISIT_NOTES)
     - Open tasks for this client (count + top 3)
     - Quick stats: diagnoses count, medications count, open tasks count

     Notes Tab

     - The post-visit notes + AI generation flow (what ClientNotesView currently
      has minus the summary/tasks columns, since those now live on Dashboard)

     Other Tabs

     - Call capture, Timeline, Care plan: embed existing components unchanged

     Files to modify

     views.jsx

     - Rewrite ClientPage: add client header + secondary sidebar + content
     routing
     - Add ClientDashboard component with summary cards
     - Slim down ClientNotesView to just the post-visit notes + generation
     section (remove the summary/tasks two-column layout since Dashboard covers
     that)

     styles.css

     - Add styles for .client-subnav (secondary sidebar within content area)

     Verification

     - Click a client in sidebar: see client header + dashboard with summary
     - Click Notes in sub-nav: see post-visit notes + AI generation
     - Click Call capture: see existing call capture
     - Click Timeline: see existing timeline
     - Click Care plan: see existing care plan
     - Sub-nav highlights correctly
  ⎿  Allowed by PermissionRequest hook

⏺ Let me implement this. First, add the sub-nav styles to CSS, then rewrite the
  ClientPage and add ClientDashboard.

❯ lets think through how we would include patient / client communication - from 
   GCM --> client to give them updates, etc.                                    

⏺ Great question. Let me think through this with you.

  A care manager like Priya communicates with multiple parties for each client:

  Who they message:
  - Family members (Dana, James, Helen) - updates, check-ins, coordination
  - Caregivers (Kate) - scheduling, daily updates
  - Providers (Dr. Hsu, pharmacies, Lakeside Manor staff) - clinical
  coordination
  - The client themselves (sometimes)

  What the communication looks like today in the prototype:
  - The DRAFT_MESSAGE is a one-off SMS to Dana
  - The inbox has inbound messages but no way to reply
  - There's no conversation thread or message history

⏺ User answered Claude's questions:
  ⎿  · What's the primary communication channel you're imagining? → Both + email
     · Should Patrona draft messages automatically for the GCM to review, or is 
     this purely manual compose? → AI drafts after events
     · Where should messaging live in the UI? → Both

⏺ Good choices. Here's how I'd structure this:

  Communication Hub Architecture:

  1. Unified thread model - Each client has conversations grouped by contact
  (Dana, Dr. Hsu, CVS, etc.). Messages can come in via SMS, email, or in-app.
  Patrona normalizes them into one thread view regardless of channel.
  2. AI-drafted messages after events - When a call ends, a visit note is saved,
   or a medication change happens, Patrona drafts an update for the relevant
  family member(s). The GCM reviews, edits if needed, and hits send. This is
  already partially mocked with DRAFT_MESSAGE.
  3. Two access points:
    - Client page > Messages tab - conversations filtered to that client
    - Workspace > Inbox - all conversations across all clients, sorted by
  recency

  For the prototype, the implementation would be:

  - Add a Messages tab to the client sub-nav
  - Show conversation threads per contact (e.g. "Dana Okafor - SMS", "Dr. Hsu -
  Email")
  - Include a compose area with channel selector (SMS / Email / In-app)
  - Show AI-drafted messages as a banner at the top ("Patrona drafted this after
   your call with Dana")
  - The global Inbox becomes the aggregate view of the same data

  Mock data needed:
  - CONVERSATIONS per client - array of threads with messages
  - Each message: sender, timestamp, channel (sms/email/app), body, read status
  - Pending AI drafts linked to events (call ended, visit note saved)

  Want me to build this out? I'd start with the client-level Messages tab and
  the mock conversation data, then upgrade the Inbox to match.
